## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, rate laws typically express reaction rates as power-law functions of concentration, with possible time-dependent effects from external forcing, autocatalysis, or complex mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order / Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (surface-catalyzed or enzyme-like kinetics)
- Second-order Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A)**2 (dual-site surface reaction)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (self-catalysis with linear and quadratic terms)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate coefficient, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous pathways)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional-order kinetics with baseline)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (dispersive kinetics in heterogeneous media)
- Exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (concentration-dependent activation energy analog)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer power-law dependence on concentration → classical reaction order (1st, 2nd, 3rd order rate laws)
- Rational function of concentration (A/(c+A)) → saturation kinetics from enzyme or surface site limitation (Michaelis-Menten type)
- Rate independent of A → zero-order kinetics indicating saturated catalyst or excess reactant conditions
- Negative coefficient on A terms → consumption/decay of reactant (typical for reactant disappearance)
- Explicit time dependence in rate law → non-isothermal conditions, photochemical forcing, or catalyst deactivation
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel reaction pathways or complex mechanisms
- Logarithmic dependence on A (log(A)) → Elovich-type kinetics for heterogeneous surface reactions
- Product of A and (1-c*A) terms → autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics with finite capacity
- Fractional (non-integer) power of A → dispersive kinetics in disordered or fractal media
- Denominator with polynomial in A → derived rate laws from quasi-steady-state approximation of intermediates
